                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> value during the discharging process can be explained by the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation and phase transition reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0070_R_d3709642e2183" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">70</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Subsequently, the formation of SEI layer, as evidenced by the cathodic peak in the CV profile, contributes to a much faster decrease of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/97ee493c-e254-4c9d-8f46-ded10af447ba/smll202404767-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202404767:smll202404767-math-0007" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202404767-math-0007.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msub>
                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> value.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0071_R_d3709642e2202" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Energy Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Then, the nearly persistent improvement of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/0193efb3-4ac2-4776-83b4-9a7d8d1a783e/smll202404767-math-0008.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202404767:smll202404767-math-0008" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202404767-math-0008.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msub>
                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> value occurs from 0.7 to 0.01&nbsp;V, possibly stemming from the refinement of crystal particles with expanded lattice during the continuous sodiation process, which results in sufficient Na<sup>+</sup> storage by conversion reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0072_R_d3709642e2224" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - Small">72</a>, <a href="#smll202404767-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0073_R_d3709642e2224" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Small Methods">73</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the charging process, the decreased <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/af0a965f-4cf4-45fa-a97b-b3d4fc457a11/smll202404767-math-0009.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202404767:smll202404767-math-0009" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202404767-math-0009.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msub>
                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> value at the first stage is attributed to the reverse conversion reaction of Na<sub>2</sub>S and Fe. After charging to 1.4&nbsp;V, the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/faa8a6f7-5cb8-4877-aba3-65a35dd501a3/smll202404767-math-0010.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202404767:smll202404767-math-0010" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202404767-math-0010.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msub>
                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^ + }}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> value begin to increase again, which is attributed to the further extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> to regenerate Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0074_R_d3709642e2266" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Small">74</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> We discover that all the variations are almost reversed in the charging process. Hence, it is suggested that the porous and robust carbon layer can protect the structural integrity and ensure a stable environment to reduce the irreversible capacity decay.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0074_R_d3709642e2272" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Small">74</a>, <a href="#smll202404767-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0075_R_d3709642e2272" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - J. Alloys Compd.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, we also investigated the more detailed reaction kinetics of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 electrode by testing the CV profiles at variable scan rates from 0.2 to 1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. As presented in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information), with the increase of scan rate, all the CV curves display similar contours, indicating the low polarization of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2. Moreover, the proportions of capacitive contribution for Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 at different scan rates can be calculated to be 74.8%, 76.7%, 83.7%, 85.3%, and 87.1% under 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. It is suggested that the high proportion of surface capacitive contribution can contribute to faster sodium storage kinetics with improved rate and cycling performances.</p>
         
         <p>To further assess the application potential of the as-prepared Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2, sodium-ion full-cells were assembled by using Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 as the anode coupled with commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode, which were denoted as Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP for simplicity as illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6a</a>. To achieve the optimal overall performance, the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 anode was presodiated at a low current density of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> for three cycles before the assembly of full-cells. Meanwhile, based on the individual charging/discharging behaviors as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6b</a>, the voltage window of full-cell device was fixed to be 0.3-3.8&nbsp;V and the mass ratio of active materials between the anode and cathode was controlled to be around 1:4.8. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6c</a> shows the GCD profiles of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP full-cell, which delivers initial charge/discharge capacities of 369/323 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> accompanied by an ICE of 87.5% based on the mass of anode active materials. The good overlap of these GCD profiles from the second cycle onward clearly indicates the excellent reversibility of the full-cell device. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6d</a> presents the good rate performance of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP full-cell with average reversible capacities of 445, 413, 367, 331, 287, 218, and 418 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at various current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and back to 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Meanwhile, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6e</a> shows the cycling performance of the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP full-cell tested at a current density of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which delivers a stable reversible capacity of 314 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 95.9% (to the second cycle) after 250 cycles. Impressively, by fast charging the full-cell in a short time of about 160 s, the logo “Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>” in a pattern of 46 red LEDs can be efficiently powered by one Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP full-cell device, as shown in the inserted photo of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6e</a>. In addition, for the the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2‖NVP full-cell device, competitive energy densities of 149, 135, 122, 111, 94, and 65&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−</sup>¹ can be achieved under power densities of 24, 68, 162, 329, 657, and 1475&nbsp;W kg<sup>−</sup>¹, respectively, which outperform those of many previously reported iron sulfide-based SIBs shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202404767-fig-0006">6f</a>, such as FeS<sub>2-x</sub>Se<sub>x</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0076_R_d3709642e2402" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeS<sub>2</sub>/CT/FeS<sub>2</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0077_R_d3709642e2412" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Green Energy Environ.">77</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeS<sub>2</sub>@G@CNF,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0078_R_d3709642e2419" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Small">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/C@ZnS/N-C@C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202404767-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202404767-bib-0064_R_d3709642e2429" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Small">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> demonstrating the promising potential of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 toward practical application in energy storage devices.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202404767-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f1a3ab71-c310-4ea3-8179-946a6a629968/smll202404767-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>

         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202404767-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202404767-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we have successfully fabricated Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC consisting of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon framework using metal coordination complex of ZnFe-NTA as functional template with a combined synthetic approach. On account of the unique core/shell architecture with regulated porous structure endowing abundant active sites, enhanced electron/Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics, as well as reinforced structural integrity, the optimal Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC electrode manifests remarkable sodium storage properties with high reversible capacity (743 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>), superior rate capability (553 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> up to 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and outstanding long-term cycling stability (98.5% retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>). Moreover, the ex situ XRD analysis reveals the intercalation and conversion reaction mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC, while in depth insights into enhanced reaction kinetics are illustrated by combined ex situ EIS and GITT investigation. Our findings in this work are expected to provide significant guidance for the rational design and development of high performance anodes for high-rate and durable sodium storage.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202404767-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202404767-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202404767-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202404767-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202404767-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202404767-sec-0070-title"> Synthesis of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/Porous N-Doped Carbon (PNC) Nanowires</h4>
                  
                  <p>First, 2&nbsp;mmol of FeCl<sub>3</sub>, 6&nbsp;mmol of nitrilotriacetic acid (NTA) and a certain amount of ZnCl<sub>2</sub> (<i>x</i> = 0, 0.2, 0.4, and 0.6&nbsp;mmol) were dissolved in a mixed solution containing 35&nbsp;mL isopropyl alcohol (IPA) and 35&nbsp;mL deionized water under vigorous stirring. Then, the above mixture was transferred into a 100&nbsp;mL Teflon-lined autoclave, heated to 180 °C and further stabilized at this temperature for 24&nbsp;h. After cooling down to room temperature, the precipitation was collected by filtration, rinsed repeatedly with deionized water and ethanol, and then dried at 80 °C in vacuum overnight, which was denoted as Fe-NTA, ZnFe-NTA-1, ZnFe-NTA-2, and ZnFe-NTA-3, respectively. Subsequently, these precursors were subjected to thermal annealing for carbonization at 700 °C for 2&nbsp;h under an Ar atmosphere to achieve the black intermediate products of Fe/PNC-0, Fe/PNC-1, Fe/PNC-2, and Fe/PNC-3, respectively. Eventually, the final products were obtained by a gas sulfurization process at 500 °C for 2&nbsp;h under a mixed Ar/H<sub>2</sub> (5 vol% H<sub>2</sub>) atmosphere with a heating rate of 3 °C min<sup>−1</sup>, which were labeled as Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-0, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-1, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2, and Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-3, respectively. In addition, to prepare the control sample of PNC, the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 sample was immersed in an aqueous HCl solution (3&nbsp;mol&nbsp;L<sup>−1</sup>) with stirring and sonication for 48&nbsp;h to remove the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles. The resulting PNC powder was washed with deionized water repeatedly and dried under vacumm overnight.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202404767-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202404767-sec-0080-title"> Material Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The morphology and microstructure of the as-prepared materials were investigated by field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FE-SEM, Zeiss Ultra 55, 3&nbsp;kV) and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM, FEI Tecnai F20, 200&nbsp;kV), respectively. The crystal structures were explored by X-ray diffraction (XRD, Bruker Advance D8) with Cu K<sub>α</sub> radiation (λ = 1.5406 Å) operated at 40&nbsp;kV and 100&nbsp;mA. The surface chemical compositions were characterized by X-ray spectroscopy (XPS, Thermo scientific K-Alpha) with a 12&nbsp;kV monochromatic Al K<sub>α</sub> X-ray source. The specific surface area and pore distribution were measured by using N<sub>2</sub> adsoprtion and desorption on a BSD-PS specific surface area and analyzer (Beishide Instrument Technology, Beijing).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202404767-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202404767-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The electrochemical performances were evaluated in CR2025-type half-cells and full-cells, which were assembled in an argon filled glovebox (H<sub>2</sub>O and O<sub>2</sub> below 0.1&nbsp;ppm). To fabricate the working electrodes in hall-cells, a homogeneous slurry prepared by mixing the active materials, Super P, and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) in a weight ratio of 7:2:1 in N-methyl pyrrolidone (NMP) was uniformly cast onto a piece of Cu foil and then dried at 80 °C overnight in a vacuum oven. The typical mass loading of active materials on the Cu foil was around 1.0&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. The half-cells were assembled by using sodium foil as the counter electrode with ether-based electrolyte (1&nbsp;M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diglyme (DME)) and glassfiber membrane separator (Whatman, GF/D). For the full-cells, commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> spread on Al foil was utilized as the cathode, and the optimal Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/PNC-2 electrode was used as the anode, which was initially presodiated by activation at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> for three cycles in a half-cell to compensate the loss of Na<sup>+</sup>. The cathode electrode was fabricated by mixing Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, Super P and PVDF with a weight ratio of 7:2:1 in NMP to form a slurry and spread onto Al foil. To balance the capacity between the cathode and anode, the N/P ratio of anode/cathode was adjusted to be about 0.83 (1:1.2), while the corresponding mass loading of active materials of anode/cathode was optimized to be about 1:4.8. Galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) tests were carried out on a Neware multichannel battery testing system. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves were recorded on a CHI 1000C electrochemical workstation. Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was applied by charging/discharging at a pulse current of 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> for 10&nbsp;min followed by resting for 30&nbsp;min. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were conducted by applying an Autolab PGSTAT 302N electrochemical workstation over a frequency range of 0.01&nbsp;Hz–100&nbsp;kHz with an amplitude of 5&nbsp;mV.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
